  78. Here is my analysis and test results for the new Gillette &#34;Flexball&#34; razor:<br /><br />▲ The razor comes with a very handy stand to hold while not being used. Fits well, stays put. The razor is very hefty--about 1.8 oz measured on my scale. By contrast, a disposable typically weighs-in less than 1 oz. I measured a Gillette disposable at 1/2 oz.<br /><br />▲ The razor body is very solid, and has a comfortable feel to it. I liked the feel of the razor body--it felt solidly constructed, and is also well-balanced. I also liked the black raised ergonomic contours on the body of the razor. Again--felt very solid and well constructed. The color of the body is black with silver trim, plus the orange Flexball.<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #1,&#34; I did not shave for several days, so that I had a 3-day beard. I washed my face with cool water, left my face wet, then applied a smooth layer of the Proglide gel. I then waited several minutes for my beard to soften. I began shaving in the easier portions of my face, where the whiskers are lighter, then proceeded to the heavier sections around my chin. The razor nicely navigated all the crags and contours without the slightest drag or snagging. The blades cut very close without the hint of scraping or cutting. I examined my face very closely after shaving, and I was very pleased with the result. The razor did an outstanding job, providing a very close, clean shave. (For the records, I do NOT have a really smooth face--it's about normal roughness.)<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #2,&#34; I had just the normal 1-day beard. I washed my face with warm water, left my face wet, then similarly applied a layer of the same gel. I waited exactly 3 1/2 minutes for the bristles to soften. This time, I paid attention to how well the razor traversed over the chin and down to the neck. I wanted to see if the rotating head of the razor could smoothly navigate this hilly territory. As before the razor did a similarly outstanding job, providing a very close and smooth shave. Thus, both the Field Tests confirm the capability of this product. It works as advertised. When I completed my shaving, I rinsed the razor, and noticed that it is somewhat difficult to get the blades entirely clean of shaving gel. With 5 blades closely spaced together, this is not a trivial feat. After cleaning, I thoroughly dried the cartridge, as I hope to extend the life of the blades.<br /><br />▲ The famous &#34;Flexball&#34; is obvious because of its bright orange color. The Flexball pivots in 2 different ways. As you hold the razor in front of you, it pivots left to right, in an angular fashion--perhaps up to 15 degrees in each direction. There are little &#34;stops&#34; on the Flexball that prevent it from rotating too far. You can see a very fine band (at first I thought it was a wire) that allows the angular pivoting. This movement is very smooth--no hitches whatsoever. There is a small screw-like pivot-point, around which the movement takes place. This fastener appears to be very solid; I doubt anything will come lose. The head of the razor also pivots forward and back, using a thin &#34;bar&#34; going into the head of the razor.<br /><br />▲ The above Flexball is very impressive engineering. It appears to operate flawlessly. All of this is to allow the razor to match the contours of your face. That's a nice way of saying, shave around all those divots and dents in your face (not that YOU have any, of course, but someone else might.) To further get around those slight detours, this product uses extremely thin, five blades that are designed to glide more smoothly; thus, there is no tugging on your skin.<br /><br />▲ Gillette also claims to incorporate a proprietary strip called the &#34;Enhanced Lubrastrip.&#34; It's the part of the cartridge that is pale green. This strip contains mineral oil and &#34;lubricating polymers.&#34; Well, my skin appreciated those &#34;polymers.&#34;<br /><br />✔ SUMMARY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris LawsonY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris Lawson

I bring this up because this has been a huge pain point for me with other blades getting clogged quickly, always right in the middle of the length of the blades.<br /><br />As for the shaving that this blade provides, it is what you would (and should) expect, a good consistent shave that does not slice your face off. Thankfully they have been in the game for quite a while and I would be pretty shocked if this was not the case. All 5-6 times I got a good shave and did not notice bleeding once. That sometimes happens to me when razors dull quickly after first 3 uses, but thankfully was not the case here.<br /><br />Like I say, in my opinion, you should expect all that. The thing I was extremely please about was how they designed the blades. With my two-three day neck growth I have not had a clog up yet that my shower spray could not clean out. I cannot tell you how happy this makes me. After the 3rd or 4th day I noticed it and was trying to figure out why. It looks like they have the razor backing right next to the blades but they have solved the problem by placing additional super tiny little gap fillers between each razor so that 1. it provides support and 2. its stops the clogging problem while allowing it to still cut evenly. Once again, GREAT product, just marketed very badly.<br /><br />The razor: Everyone knows the Gilette Fusion is already a great razor: It cuts hair very well without cutting the skin. This latest variation puts a pivot on the end of the razor handle. The pivot lets the razor follow the skin even more closely for an even eaiser, better shave. It's a &#34;no brainer&#34; - this is a great product!<br /><br />Now for all the marketing problems - where do I start? Actually, they got one thing right. Last year I reviewed the Gilette Fusion ProGlide Styler and complained about the packaging. This time they have a package that is stylish yet easy to open and somewhat eco-friendly. Now for the problems:<br /><br />FlexBall: BAD name for the pivoting end. It's not actually a ball, it's just a side to side pivot made to look like a ball. I was actually MORE impressed with it once I found out it wasn't really a ball, because it means the razor doesn't flop all over your face, it just gently pivots, so I still feel I'm in control.<br /><br />SilverTouch: Gilette markets both Silver and non-Silver versions. I went to their website, and I can't figure out what the difference is.<br /><br />Manual: Gilette markets both &#34;Manual&#34; and &#34;Power&#34; versions. The power version has a battery and it vibrates the razor. I've tried the power version before and it doesn't really do anything for me... it's not an electric razor, it's just a manual razor that vibrates. I don't think it cuts any differently. It would be nice if Gilette would further explain the benefits of the power version.<br /><br />The Name: WAY TOO LONG. If I wrote &#34;Gilette Fusion&#34; on a shopping list for someone else to buy, I probably would end up with the wrong thing - there's lots of Gilette Fusions now. The only way to know for sure is to go to the store myself and try to pick out the exact right product with the exact right options. Why not have a simple name like &#34;Gilette Fusion 5000&#34; or &#34;Gilette Fusion 6000&#34;?<br /><br />The Options: As a follow-up, why offer so many options anyway? Does it really cost that much more to add the FlexBall to the razor - why not just give it (and ALL of the best options) to everyone? The razor might cost a little more, but you only have to buy it once. Or at least that is what Gilette would want you to believe. In reality, what they seem to be doing is coming up with one exciting new option a year, so each year you have to buy a new razor anyway to keep up with the latest options. Clever way to keep consumers buying, but not nice on the pocketbook.<br /><br />In short, Gilette needs to come up with a far simpler product name and maybe only 2 or 3 variations, and that's it - keep it simple. Otherwise, I'll be staring at a dozen options on the shelf and looking at all the marketing lingo and trying to figure out what I actually need. Hidden behind all this mess is a terrific product; it's a shame that their marketing department has to make it so complicated!

I've used safety razors in the past, and when using a safety razor, you want a light touch and loose grip so as not to put much pressure on the skin, which results in nicks and cuts. That technique translates quite well with the Proglide Silvertouch. Now, on to the shave. I'll preface this by saying I use the Art of Shaving lavender pre-shave oil, shaving cream, and badger hair brush. I built up a week of beard growth to give this a proper test. After my pre-shave routine, it was time to unleash this razor and see what it could do. First thoughts, the weight of the razor, in combination with good technique, feels great against the skin. My neck is pretty sensitive when it comes to shaving, but I had no issues here. One thing I noticed, the proglide strip, in combination with my pre-shave oil and shaving cream, was too goopy for my liking. I wouldn't knock any stars off of the review, as I'm sure without the oil, it would be a non-issue. As for the flexball head, I normally have issues around my jawline, and have to make a few passes to get a proper shave. With the flexball head, however, Ihad no problems getting the hair on the first pass. This is exciting for me, as normally my skin gets irritated with multiple passes and I always dread the jawline. I would say that the head really did contour for maximum contact. Score one for Gillette. The precision razor on the back is the same as I've experienced with previous Gillette razors. No improvement there. Overall, I'd have to say that this is the best razor that I've ever used. After two weeks, this razor is still treating me right, and is as great a shave as the first time. Then again, I only shave two times a week. This razor really does live up to the hype, and I'm very happy with the decision to get it.
